I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Context cancellation causes a goroutine leak (possibly intermittent)
### Problem statement

When running our integration tests suite with https://github.com/uber-go/goleak, it sometimes reports a goroutine leak in:

```
 manager_envtest_test.go:84: found unexpected goroutines:
          [Goroutine 12886 in state sync.WaitGroup.Wait, with sync.runtime_SemacquireWaitGroup on top of the stack:
          sync.runtime_SemacquireWaitGroup(0xc000cdc830?)
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/golang.org/toolchain@v0.0.1-go1.24.1.linux-amd64/src/runtime/sema.go:110 +0x25
          sync.(*WaitGroup).Wait(0xc000cdc830)
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/golang.org/toolchain@v0.0.1-go1.24.1.linux-amd64/src/sync/waitgroup.go:118 +0x89
          sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*controllerManager).engageStopProcedure.func3.(*runnableGroup).StopAndWait.3.2()
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:307 +0x99
          created by sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*controllerManager).engageStopProcedure.func3.(*runnableGroup).StopAndWait.3 in goroutine 12666
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:304 +0x213
           Goroutine 12791 in state chan send, with sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile.func1 on top of the stack:
          sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile.func1(0xc00115d940)
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:227 +0x1f8
          created by sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile in goroutine 12615
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:210 +0x245
           Goroutine 12838 in state chan send, with sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile.func1 on top of the stack:
          sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile.func1(0xc00115dd00)
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:227 +0x1f8
          created by sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager.(*runnableGroup).reconcile in goroutine 12615
          	/home/runner/go/pkg/mod/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime@v0.20.4/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go:210 +0x245
          ]
```

After quick glance at the code, it would seem that `controllerManager` passes its `errChan` to its `runnableGroup`s.

When runnables fail, they propagate the error through that error channel in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/blob/dcb8a6a8d7ed700d4590f11fac171f766f54ea3c/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go#L227.

If I'm looking at this correctly, when context is done, the `errChan` is not drained in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/blob/5af1f3ebd472b62a4a708ad3aa2d252489b91b27/pkg/manager/internal.go#L467-L469 and thus runnable groups cannot send their errors in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/blob/dcb8a6a8d7ed700d4590f11fac171f766f54ea3c/pkg/manager/runnable_group.go#L224.

### Proposed solution

Drain the `cm.errChan` in `case <-ctx.Done()` branch at https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/blob/5af1f3ebd472b62a4a708ad3aa2d252489b91b27/pkg/manager/internal.go#L466-L473

</pr_description>

    63	type controllerManager struct {
    64	        sync.Mutex
    65	        started bool
    66	
    67	        stopProcedureEngaged *int64
    68	        errChan              chan error
    69	        runnables            *runnables
    70	
    71	        // cluster holds a variety of methods to interact with a cluster. Required.
    72	        cluster cluster.Cluster
    73	
    74	        // recorderProvider is used to generate event recorders that will be injected into Controllers
    75	        // (and EventHandlers, Sources and Predicates).
    76	        recorderProvider *intrec.Provider
    77	
    78	        // resourceLock forms the basis for leader election
    79	        resourceLock resourcelock.Interface
    80	
    81	        // leaderElectionReleaseOnCancel defines if the manager should step back from the leader lease
    82	        // on shutdown
    83	        leaderElectionReleaseOnCancel bool
    84	
    85	        // metricsServer is used to serve prometheus metrics
    86	        metricsServer metricsserver.Server
    87	
    88	        // healthProbeListener is used to serve liveness probe
    89	        healthProbeListener net.Listener
    90	
    91	        // Readiness probe endpoint name
    92	        readinessEndpointName string
    93	
    94	        // Liveness probe endpoint name
    95	        livenessEndpointName string
    96	
    97	        // Readyz probe handler
    98	        readyzHandler *healthz.Handler
    99	
   100	        // Healthz probe handler
   101	        healthzHandler *healthz.Handler
   102	
   103	        // pprofListener is used to serve pprof
   104	        pprofListener net.Listener
   105	
   106	        // controllerConfig are the global controller options.
   107	        controllerConfig config.Controller
   108	
   109	        // Logger is the logger that should be used by this manager.
   110	        // If none is set, it defaults to log.Log global logger.
   111	        logger logr.Logger
   112	
   113	        // leaderElectionStopped is an internal channel used to signal the stopping procedure that the
   114	        // LeaderElection.Run(...) function has returned and the shutdown can proceed.
   115	        leaderElectionStopped chan struct{}
   116	
   117	        // leaderElectionCancel is used to cancel the leader election. It is distinct from internalStopper,
   118	        // because for safety reasons we need to os.Exit() when we lose the leader election, meaning that
   119	        // it must be deferred until after gracefulShutdown is done.
   120	        leaderElectionCancel context.CancelFunc
   121	
   122	        // elected is closed when this manager becomes the leader of a group of
   123	        // managers, either because it won a leader election or because no leader
   124	        // election was configured.
   125	        elected chan struct{}
   126	
   127	        webhookServer webhook.Server
   128	        // webhookServerOnce will be called in GetWebhookServer() to optionally initialize
   129	        // webhookServer if unset, and Add() it to controllerManager.
   130	        webhookServerOnce sync.Once
   131	
   132	        // leaderElectionID is the name of the resource that leader election
   133	        // will use for holding the leader lock.
   134	        leaderElectionID string
   135	        // leaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will
   136	        // wait to force acquire leadership.
   137	        leaseDuration time.Duration
   138	        // renewDeadline is the duration that the acting controlplane will retry
   139	        // refreshing leadership before giving up.
   140	        renewDeadline time.Duration
   141	        // retryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait
   142	        // between tries of actions.
   143	        retryPeriod time.Duration
   144	
   145	        // gracefulShutdownTimeout is the duration given to runnable to stop
   146	        // before the manager actually returns on stop.
   147	        gracefulShutdownTimeout time.Duration
   148	
   149	        // onStoppedLeading is callled when the leader election lease is lost.
   150	        // It can be overridden for tests.
   151	        onStoppedLeading func()
   152	
   153	        // shutdownCtx is the context that can be used during shutdown. It will be cancelled
   154	        // after the gracefulShutdownTimeout ended. It must not be accessed before internalStop
   155	        // is closed because it will be nil.
   156	        shutdownCtx context.Context
   157	
   158	        internalCtx    context.Context
   159	        internalCancel context.CancelFunc
   160	
   161	        // internalProceduresStop channel is used internally to the manager when coordinating
   162	        // the proper shutdown of servers. This channel is also used for dependency injection.
   163	        internalProceduresStop chan struct{}
   164	}

   166	type hasCache interface {
   167	        Runnable

   171	// Add sets dependencies on i, and adds it to the list of Runnables to start.
   172	func (cm *controllerManager) Add(r Runnable) error {
   173	        cm.Lock()
   174	        defer cm.Unlock()
   175	        return cm.add(r)
   176	}
   177	
   178	func (cm *controllerManager) add(r Runnable) error {
   179	        return cm.runnables.Add(r)
   180	}
   181	
   182	// AddMetricsServerExtraHandler adds extra handler served on path to the http server that serves metrics.
   183	func (cm *controllerManager) AddMetricsServerExtraHandler(path string, handler http.Handler) error {
   184	        cm.Lock()
   185	        defer cm.Unlock()
   186	        if cm.started {
   187	                return fmt.Errorf("unable to add new metrics handler because metrics endpoint has already been created")
   188	        }
   189	        if cm.metricsServer == nil {
   190	                cm.GetLogger().Info("warn: metrics server is currently disabled, registering extra handler will be ignored", "path", path)
   191	                return nil
   192	        }
   193	        if err := cm.metricsServer.AddExtraHandler(path, handler); err != nil {
   194	                return err
   195	        }
   196	        cm.logger.V(2).Info("Registering metrics http server extra handler", "path", path)
   197	        return nil
   198	}
   199	
   200	// AddHealthzCheck allows you to add Healthz checker.
   201	func (cm *controllerManager) AddHealthzCheck(name string, check healthz.Checker) error {
   202	        cm.Lock()
   203	        defer cm.Unlock()
   204	
   205	        if cm.started {
   206	                return fmt.Errorf("unable to add new checker because healthz endpoint has already been created")
   207	        }
   208	
   209	        if cm.healthzHandler == nil {
   210	                cm.healthzHandler = &healthz.Handler{Checks: map[string]healthz.Checker{}}
   211	        }
   212	
   213	        cm.healthzHandler.Checks[name] = check
   214	        return nil
   215	}
   216	
   217	// AddReadyzCheck allows you to add Readyz checker.
   218	func (cm *controllerManager) AddReadyzCheck(name string, check healthz.Checker) error {
   219	        cm.Lock()
   220	        defer cm.Unlock()
   221	
   222	        if cm.started {
   223	                return fmt.Errorf("unable to add new checker because healthz endpoint has already been created")
   224	        }
   225	
   226	        if cm.readyzHandler == nil {
   227	                cm.readyzHandler = &healthz.Handler{Checks: map[string]healthz.Checker{}}
   228	        }
   229	
   230	        cm.readyzHandler.Checks[name] = check
   231	        return nil
   232	}

   270	func (cm *controllerManager) GetWebhookServer() webhook.Server {
   271	        cm.webhookServerOnce.Do(func() {
   272	                if cm.webhookServer == nil {
   273	                        panic("webhook should not be nil")
   274	                }
   275	                if err := cm.Add(cm.webhookServer); err != nil {
   276	                        panic(fmt.Sprintf("unable to add webhook server to the controller manager: %s", err))
   277	                }
   278	        })
   279	        return cm.webhookServer
   280	}

   283	        return cm.logger

   287	        return cm.controllerConfig

   290	func (cm *controllerManager) addHealthProbeServer() error {
   291	        mux := http.NewServeMux()
   292	        srv := httpserver.New(mux)
   293	
   294	        if cm.readyzHandler != nil {
   295	                mux.Handle(cm.readinessEndpointName, http.StripPrefix(cm.readinessEndpointName, cm.readyzHandler))
   296	                // Append '/' suffix to handle subpaths
   297	                mux.Handle(cm.readinessEndpointName+"/", http.StripPrefix(cm.readinessEndpointName, cm.readyzHandler))
   298	        }
   299	        if cm.healthzHandler != nil {
   300	                mux.Handle(cm.livenessEndpointName, http.StripPrefix(cm.livenessEndpointName, cm.healthzHandler))
   301	                // Append '/' suffix to handle subpaths
   302	                mux.Handle(cm.livenessEndpointName+"/", http.StripPrefix(cm.livenessEndpointName, cm.healthzHandler))
   303	        }
   304	
   305	        return cm.add(&Server{
   306	                Name:     "health probe",
   307	                Server:   srv,
   308	                Listener: cm.healthProbeListener,
   309	        })
   310	}
   311	
   312	func (cm *controllerManager) addPprofServer() error {
   313	        mux := http.NewServeMux()
   314	        srv := httpserver.New(mux)
   315	
   316	        mux.HandleFunc("/debug/pprof/", pprof.Index)
   317	        mux.HandleFunc("/debug/pprof/cmdline", pprof.Cmdline)
   318	        mux.HandleFunc("/debug/pprof/profile", pprof.Profile)
   319	        mux.HandleFunc("/debug/pprof/symbol", pprof.Symbol)
   320	        mux.HandleFunc("/debug/pprof/trace", pprof.Trace)
   321	
   322	        return cm.add(&Server{
   323	                Name:     "pprof",
   324	                Server:   srv,
   325	                Listener: cm.pprofListener,
   326	        })
   327	}
   328	
   329	// Start starts the manager and waits indefinitely.
   330	// There is only two ways to have start return:
   331	// An error has occurred during in one of the internal operations,
   332	// such as leader election, cache start, webhooks, and so on.
   333	// Or, the context is cancelled.
   334	func (cm *controllerManager) Start(ctx context.Context) (err error) {
   335	        cm.Lock()
   336	        if cm.started {
   337	                cm.Unlock()
   338	                return errors.New("manager already started")
   339	        }
   340	        cm.started = true
   341	
   342	        var ready bool
   343	        defer func() {
   344	                // Only unlock the manager if we haven't reached
   345	                // the internal readiness condition.
   346	                if !ready {
   347	                        cm.Unlock()
   348	                }
   349	        }()
   350	
   351	        // Initialize the internal context.
   352	        cm.internalCtx, cm.internalCancel = context.WithCancel(ctx)
   353	
   354	        // Leader elector must be created before defer that contains engageStopProcedure function
   355	        // https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/issues/2873
   356	        var leaderElector *leaderelection.LeaderElector
   357	        if cm.resourceLock != nil {
   358	                leaderElector, err = cm.initLeaderElector()
   359	                if err != nil {
   360	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed during initialization leader election process: %w", err)
   361	                }
   362	        }
   363	
   364	        // This chan indicates that stop is complete, in other words all runnables have returned or timeout on stop request
   365	        stopComplete := make(chan struct{})
   366	        defer close(stopComplete)
   367	        // This must be deferred after closing stopComplete, otherwise we deadlock.
   368	        defer func() {
   369	                // https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod.s3.amazonaws.com/images/gettyimages-459889618-1533579787.jpg
   370	                stopErr := cm.engageStopProcedure(stopComplete)
   371	                if stopErr != nil {
   372	                        if err != nil {
   373	                                // Utilerrors.Aggregate allows to use errors.Is for all contained errors
   374	                                // whereas fmt.Errorf allows wrapping at most one error which means the
   375	                                // other one can not be found anymore.
   376	                                err = kerrors.NewAggregate([]error{err, stopErr})
   377	                        } else {
   378	                                err = stopErr
   379	                        }
   380	                }
   381	        }()
   382	
   383	        // Add the cluster runnable.
   384	        if err := cm.add(cm.cluster); err != nil {
   385	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to add cluster to runnables: %w", err)
   386	        }
   387	
   388	        // Metrics should be served whether the controller is leader or not.
   389	        // (If we don't serve metrics for non-leaders, prometheus will still scrape
   390	        // the pod but will get a connection refused).
   391	        if cm.metricsServer != nil {
   392	                // Note: We are adding the metrics server directly to HTTPServers here as matching on the
   393	                // metricsserver.Server interface in cm.runnables.Add would be very brittle.
   394	                if err := cm.runnables.HTTPServers.Add(cm.metricsServer, nil); err != nil {
   395	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add metrics server: %w", err)
   396	                }
   397	        }
   398	
   399	        // Serve health probes.
   400	        if cm.healthProbeListener != nil {
   401	                if err := cm.addHealthProbeServer(); err != nil {
   402	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add health probe server: %w", err)
   403	                }
   404	        }
   405	
   406	        // Add pprof server
   407	        if cm.pprofListener != nil {
   408	                if err := cm.addPprofServer(); err != nil {
   409	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add pprof server: %w", err)
   410	                }
   411	        }
   412	
   413	        // First start any HTTP servers, which includes health probes, metrics and profiling if enabled.
   414	        //
   415	        // WARNING: HTTPServers includes the health probes, which MUST start before any cache is populated, otherwise
   416	        // it would block conversion webhooks to be ready for serving which make the cache never get ready.
   417	        logCtx := logr.NewContext(cm.internalCtx, cm.logger)
   418	        if err := cm.runnables.HTTPServers.Start(logCtx); err != nil {
   419	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start HTTP servers: %w", err)
   420	        }
   421	
   422	        // Start any webhook servers, which includes conversion, validation, and defaulting
   423	        // webhooks that are registered.
   424	        //
   425	        // WARNING: Webhooks MUST start before any cache is populated, otherwise there is a race condition
   426	        // between conversion webhooks and the cache sync (usually initial list) which causes the webhooks
   427	        // to never start because no cache can be populated.
   428	        if err := cm.runnables.Webhooks.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   429	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start webhooks: %w", err)
   430	        }
   431	
   432	        // Start and wait for caches.
   433	        if err := cm.runnables.Caches.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   434	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start caches: %w", err)
   435	        }
   436	
   437	        // Start the non-leaderelection Runnables after the cache has synced.
   438	        if err := cm.runnables.Others.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   439	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start other runnables: %w", err)
   440	        }
   441	
   442	        // Start the leader election and all required runnables.
   443	        {
   444	                ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
   445	                cm.leaderElectionCancel = cancel
   446	                if leaderElector != nil {
   447	                        // Start the leader elector process
   448	                        go func() {
   449	                                leaderElector.Run(ctx)
   450	                                <-ctx.Done()
   451	                                close(cm.leaderElectionStopped)
   452	                        }()
   453	                } else {
   454	                        go func() {
   455	                                // Treat not having leader election enabled the same as being elected.
   456	                                if err := cm.startLeaderElectionRunnables(); err != nil {
   457	                                        cm.errChan <- err
   458	                                }
   459	                                close(cm.elected)
   460	                        }()
   461	                }
   462	        }
   463	
   464	        ready = true
   465	        cm.Unlock()
   466	        select {
   467	        case <-ctx.Done():
   468	                // We are done
   469	                return nil
   470	        case err := <-cm.errChan:
   471	                // Error starting or running a runnable
   472	                return err
   473	        }
   474	}
   475	
   476	// engageStopProcedure signals all runnables to stop, reads potential errors
   477	// from the errChan and waits for them to end. It must not be called more than once.
   478	func (cm *controllerManager) engageStopProcedure(stopComplete <-chan struct{}) error {
   479	        if !atomic.CompareAndSwapInt64(cm.stopProcedureEngaged, 0, 1) {
   480	                return errors.New("stop procedure already engaged")
   481	        }
   482	
   483	        // Populate the shutdown context, this operation MUST be done before
   484	        // closing the internalProceduresStop channel.
   485	        //
   486	        // The shutdown context immediately expires if the gracefulShutdownTimeout is not set.
   487	        var shutdownCancel context.CancelFunc
   488	        if cm.gracefulShutdownTimeout < 0 {
   489	                // We want to wait forever for the runnables to stop.
   490	                cm.shutdownCtx, shutdownCancel = cont<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you.     15	// readyRunnable encapsulates a runnable with
    16	// a ready check.
    17	type readyRunnable struct {
    18	        Runnable
    19	        Check       runnableCheck
    20	        signalReady bool
    21	}
    22	
    23	// runnableCheck can be passed to Add() to let the runnable group determine that a
    24	// runnable is ready. A runnable check should block until a runnable is ready,
    25	// if the returned result is false, the runnable is considered not ready and failed.
    26	type runnableCheck func(ctx context.Context) bool
    27	
    28	// runnables handles all the runnables for a manager by grouping them accordingly to their
    29	// type (webhooks, caches etc.).
    30	type runnables struct {
    31	        HTTPServers    *runnableGroup
    32	        Webhooks       *runnableGroup
    33	        Caches         *runnableGroup
    34	        LeaderElection *runnableGroup
    35	        Others         *runnableGroup
    36	}
    37	
    38	// newRunnables creates a new runnables object.
    39	func newRunnables(baseContext BaseContextFunc, errChan chan error) *runnables {
    40	        return &runnables{
    41	                HTTPServers:    newRunnableGroup(baseContext, errChan),
    42	                Webhooks:       newRunnableGroup(baseContext, errChan),
    43	                Caches:         newRunnableGroup(baseContext, errChan),
    44	                LeaderElection: newRunnableGroup(baseContext, errChan),
    45	                Others:         newRunnableGroup(baseContext, errChan),
    46	        }
    47	}
    48	
    49	// Add adds a runnable to closest group of runnable that they belong to.
    50	//
    51	// Add should be able to be called before and after Start, but not after StopAndWait.
    52	// Add should return an error when called during StopAndWait.
    53	// The runnables added before Start are started when Start is called.
    54	// The runnables added after Start are started directly.
    55	func (r *runnables) Add(fn Runnable) error {
    56	        switch runnable := fn.(type) {
    57	        case *Server:
    58	                if runnable.NeedLeaderElection() {
    59	                        return r.LeaderElection.Add(fn, nil)
    60	                }
    61	                return r.HTTPServers.Add(fn, nil)
    62	        case hasCache:
    63	                return r.Caches.Add(fn, func(ctx context.Context) bool {
    64	                        return runnable.GetCache().WaitForCacheSync(ctx)
    65	                })
    66	        case webhook.Server:
    67	                return r.Webhooks.Add(fn, nil)
    68	        case LeaderElectionRunnable:
    69	                if !runnable.NeedLeaderElection() {
    70	                        return r.Others.Add(fn, nil)
    71	                }
    72	                return r.LeaderElection.Add(fn, nil)
    73	        default:
    74	                return r.LeaderElection.Add(fn, nil)
    75	        }
    76	}
    77	
    78	// runnableGroup manages a group of runnables that are
    79	// meant to be running together until StopAndWait is called.
    80	//
    81	// Runnables can be added to a group after the group has started
    82	// but not after it's stopped or while shutting down.
    83	type runnableGroup struct {
    84	        ctx    context.Context
    85	        cancel context.CancelFunc
    86	
    87	        start        sync.Mutex
    88	        startOnce    sync.Once
    89	        started      bool
    90	        startQueue   []*readyRunnable
    91	        startReadyCh chan *readyRunnable
    92	
    93	        stop     sync.RWMutex
    94	        stopOnce sync.Once
    95	        stopped  bool
    96	
    97	        // errChan is the error channel passed by the caller
    98	        // when the group is created.
    99	        // All errors are forwarded to this channel once they occur.
   100	        errChan chan error
   101	
   102	        // ch is the internal channel where the runnables are read off from.
   103	        ch chan *readyRunnable
   104	
   105	        // wg is an internal sync.WaitGroup that allows us to properly stop
   106	        // and wait for all the runnables to finish before returning.
   107	        wg *sync.WaitGroup
   108	}
   109	
   110	func newRunnableGroup(baseContext BaseContextFunc, errChan chan error) *runnableGroup {
   111	        r := &runnableGroup{
   112	                startReadyCh: make(chan *readyRunnable),
   113	                errChan:      errChan,
   114	                ch:           make(chan *readyRunnable),
   115	                wg:           new(sync.WaitGroup),
   116	        }
   117	
   118	        r.ctx, r.cancel = context.WithCancel(baseContext())
   119	        return r
   120	}
   121	
   122	// Started returns true if the group has started.
   123	func (r *runnableGroup) Started() bool {
   124	        r.start.Lock()
   125	        defer r.start.Unlock()
   126	        return r.started
   127	}
   128	
   129	// Start starts the group and waits for all
   130	// initially registered runnables to start.
   131	// It can only be called once, subsequent calls have no effect.
   132	func (r *runnableGroup) Start(ctx context.Context) error {
   133	        var retErr error
   134	
   135	        r.startOnce.Do(func() {
   136	                defer close(r.startReadyCh)
   137	
   138	                // Start the internal reconciler.
   139	                go r.reconcile()
   140	
   141	                // Start the group and queue up all
   142	                // the runnables that were added prior.
   143	                r.start.Lock()
   144	                r.started = true
   145	                for _, rn := range r.startQueue {
   146	                        rn.signalReady = true
   147	                        r.ch <- rn
   148	                }
   149	                r.start.Unlock()
   150	
   151	                // If we don't have any queue, return.
   152	                if len(r.startQueue) == 0 {
   153	                        return
   154	                }
   155	
   156	                // Wait for all runnables to signal.
   157	                for {
   158	                        select {
   159	                        case <-ctx.Done():
   160	                                if err := ctx.Err(); !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {
   161	                                        retErr = err
   162	                                }
   163	                        case rn := <-r.startReadyCh:
   164	                                for i, existing := range r.startQueue {
   165	                                        if existing == rn {
   166	                                                // Remove the item from the start queue.
   167	                                                r.startQueue = append(r.startQueue[:i], r.startQueue[i+1:]...)
   168	                                                break
   169	                                        }
   170	                                }
   171	                                // We're done waiting if the queue is empty, return.
   172	                                if len(r.startQueue) == 0 {
   173	                                        return
   174	                                }
   175	                        }
   176	                }
   177	        })
   178	
   179	        return retErr
   180	}
   181	
   182	// reconcile is our main entrypoint for every runnable added
   183	// to this group. Its primary job is to read off the internal channel
   184	// and schedule runnables while tracking their state.
   185	func (r *runnableGroup) reconcile() {
   186	        for runnable := range r.ch {
   187	                // Handle stop.
   188	                // If the shutdown has been called we want to avoid
   189	                // adding new goroutines to the WaitGroup because Wait()
   190	                // panics if Add() is called after it.
   191	                {
   192	                        r.stop.RLock()
   193	                        if r.stopped {
   194	                                // Drop any runnables if we're stopped.
   195	                                r.errChan <- errRunnableGroupStopped
   196	                                r.stop.RUnlock()
   197	                                continue
   198	                        }
   199	
   200	                        // Why is this here?
   201	                        // When StopAndWait is called, if a runnable is in the process
   202	                        // of being added, we could end up in a situation where
   203	                        // the WaitGroup is incremented while StopAndWait has called Wait(),
   204	                        // which would result in a panic.
   205	                        r.wg.Add(1)
   206	                        r.stop.RUnlock()
   207	                }
   208	
   209	                // Start the runnable.
   210	                go func(rn *readyRunnable) {
   211	                        go func() {
   212	                                if rn.Check(r.ctx) {
   213	                                        if rn.signalReady {
   214	                                                r.startReadyCh <- rn
   215	                                        }
   216	                                }
   217	                        }()
   218	
   219	                        // If we return, the runnable ended cleanly
   220	                        // or returned an error to the channel.
   221	                        //
   222	                        // We should always decrement the WaitGroup here.
   223	                        defer r.wg.Done()
   224	
   225	                        // Start the runnable.
   226	                        if err := rn.Start(r.ctx); err != nil {
   227	                                r.errChan <- err
   228	                        }
   229	                }(runnable)
   230	        }
   231	}
   232	
   233	// Add should be able to be called before and after Start, but not after StopAndWait.
   234	// Add should return an error when called during StopAndWait.
   235	func (r *runnableGroup) Add(rn Runnable, ready runnableCheck) error {
   236	        r.stop.RLock()
   237	        if r.stopped {
   238	                r.stop.RUnlock()
   239	                return errRunnableGroupStopped
   240	        }
   241	        r.stop.RUnlock()
   242	
   243	        if ready == nil {
   244	                ready = func(_ context.Context) bool { return true }
   245	        }
   246	
   247	        readyRunnable := &readyRunnable{
   248	                Runnable: rn,
   249	                Check:    ready,
   250	        }
   251	
   252	        // Handle start.
   253	        // If the overall runnable group isn't started yet
   254	        // we want to buffer the runnables and let Start()
   255	        // queue them up again later.
   256	        {
   257	                r.start.Lock()
   258	
   259	                // Check if we're already started.
   260	                if !r.started {
   261	                        // Store the runnable in the internal if not.
   262	                        r.startQueue = append(r.startQueue, readyRunnable)
   263	                        r.start.Unlock()
   264	                        return nil
   265	                }
   266	                r.start.Unlock()
   267	        }
   268	
   269	        // Recheck if we're stopped and hold the readlock, given that the stop and start can be called
   270	        // at the same time, we can end up in a situation where the runnable is added
   271	        // after the group is stopped and the channel is closed.
   272	        r.stop.RLock()
   273	        defer r.stop.RUnlock()
   274	        if r.stopped {
   275	                return errRunnableGroupStopped
   276	        }
   277	
   278	        // Enqueue the runnable.
   279	        r.ch <- readyRunnable
   280	        return nil
   281	}
   282	
   283	// StopAndWait waits for all the runnables to finish before returning.
   284	func (r *runnableGroup) StopAndWait(ctx context.Context) {
   285	        r.stopOnce.Do(func() {
   286	                // Close the reconciler channel once we're done.
   287	                defer func() {
   288	                        r.stop.Lock()
   289	                        close(r.ch)
   290	                        r.stop.Unlock()
   291	                }()
   292	
   293	                _ = r.Start(ctx)
   294	                r.stop.Lock()
   295	                // Store the stopped variable so we don't accept any new
   296	                // runnables for the time being.
   297	                r.stopped = true
   298	                r.stop.Unlock()
   299	
   300	                // Cancel the internal channel.
   301	                r.cancel()
   302	
   303	                done := make(chan struct{})
   304	                go func() {
   305	                        defer close(done)
   306	                        // Wait for all the runnables to finish.
   307	                        r.wg.Wait()
   308	                }()
   309	
   310	                select {
   311	                case <-done:
   312	                        // We're done, exit.
   313	                case <-ctx.Done():
   314	                        // Calling context has expired, exit.
   315	                }
   316	        })
   317	}

   476	// engageStopProcedure signals all runnables to stop, reads potential errors
   477	// from the errChan and waits for them to end. It must not be called more than once.
   478	func (cm *controllerManager) engageStopProcedure(stopComplete <-chan struct{}) error {
   479	        if !atomic.CompareAndSwapInt64(cm.stopProcedureEngaged, 0, 1) {
   480	                return errors.New("stop procedure already engaged")
   481	        }
   482	
   483	        // Populate the shutdown context, this operation MUST be done before
   484	        // closing the internalProceduresStop channel.
   485	        //
   486	        // The shutdown context immediately expires if the gracefulShutdownTimeout is not set.
   487	        var shutdownCancel context.CancelFunc
   488	        if cm.gracefulShutdownTimeout < 0 {
   489	                // We want to wait forever for the runnables to stop.
   490	                cm.shutdownCtx, shutdownCancel = context.WithCancel(context.Background())
   491	        } else {
   492	                cm.shutdownCtx, shutdownCancel = context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), cm.gracefulShutdownTimeout)
   493	        }
   494	        defer shutdownCancel()
   495	
   496	        // Start draining the errors before acquiring the lock to make sure we don't deadlock
   497	        // if something that has the lock is blocked on trying to write into the unbuffered
   498	        // channel after something else already wrote into it.
   499	        var closeOnce sync.Once
   500	        go func() {
   501	                for {
   502	                        // Closing in the for loop is required to avoid race conditions between
   503	                        // the closure of all internal procedures and making sure to have a reader off the error channel.
   504	                        closeOnce.Do(func() {
   505	                                // Cancel the internal stop channel and wait for the procedures to stop and complete.
   506	                                close(cm.internalProceduresStop)
   507	                                cm.internalCancel()
   508	                        })
   509	                        select {
   510	                        case err := <-cm.errChan:
   511	                                if !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {
   512	                                        cm.logger.Error(err, "error received after stop sequence was engaged")
   513	                                }

   329	// Start starts the manager and waits indefinitely.
   330	// There is only two ways to have start return:
   331	// An error has occurred during in one of the internal operations,
   332	// such as leader election, cache start, webhooks, and so on.
   333	// Or, the context is cancelled.
   334	func (cm *controllerManager) Start(ctx context.Context) (err error) {
   335	        cm.Lock()
   336	        if cm.started {
   337	                cm.Unlock()
   338	                return errors.New("manager already started")
   339	        }
   340	        cm.started = true
   341	
   342	        var ready bool
   343	        defer func() {
   344	                // Only unlock the manager if we haven't reached
   345	                // the internal readiness condition.
   346	                if !ready {
   347	                        cm.Unlock()
   348	                }
   349	        }()
   350	
   351	        // Initialize the internal context.
   352	        cm.internalCtx, cm.internalCancel = context.WithCancel(ctx)
   353	
   354	        // Leader elector must be created before defer that contains engageStopProcedure function
   355	        // https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/controller-runtime/issues/2873
   356	        var leaderElector *leaderelection.LeaderElector
   357	        if cm.resourceLock != nil {
   358	                leaderElector, err = cm.initLeaderElector()
   359	                if err != nil {
   360	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed during initialization leader election process: %w", err)
   361	                }
   362	        }
   363	
   364	        // This chan indicates that stop is complete, in other words all runnables have returned or timeout on stop request
   365	        stopComplete := make(chan struct{})
   366	        defer close(stopComplete)
   367	        // This must be deferred after closing stopComplete, otherwise we deadlock.
   368	        defer func() {
   369	                // https://hips.hearstapps.com/hmg-prod.s3.amazonaws.com/images/gettyimages-459889618-1533579787.jpg
   370	                stopErr := cm.engageStopProcedure(stopComplete)
   371	                if stopErr != nil {
   372	                        if err != nil {
   373	                                // Utilerrors.Aggregate allows to use errors.Is for all contained errors
   374	                                // whereas fmt.Errorf allows wrapping at most one error which means the
   375	                                // other one can not be found anymore.
   376	                                err = kerrors.NewAggregate([]error{err, stopErr})
   377	                        } else {
   378	                                err = stopErr
   379	                        }
   380	                }
   381	        }()
   382	
   383	        // Add the cluster runnable.
   384	        if err := cm.add(cm.cluster); err != nil {
   385	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to add cluster to runnables: %w", err)
   386	        }
   387	
   388	        // Metrics should be served whether the controller is leader or not.
   389	        // (If we don't serve metrics for non-leaders, prometheus will still scrape
   390	        // the pod but will get a connection refused).
   391	        if cm.metricsServer != nil {
   392	                // Note: We are adding the metrics server directly to HTTPServers here as matching on the
   393	                // metricsserver.Server interface in cm.runnables.Add would be very brittle.
   394	                if err := cm.runnables.HTTPServers.Add(cm.metricsServer, nil); err != nil {
   395	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add metrics server: %w", err)
   396	                }
   397	        }
   398	
   399	        // Serve health probes.
   400	        if cm.healthProbeListener != nil {
   401	                if err := cm.addHealthProbeServer(); err != nil {
   402	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add health probe server: %w", err)
   403	                }
   404	        }
   405	
   406	        // Add pprof server
   407	        if cm.pprofListener != nil {
   408	                if err := cm.addPprofServer(); err != nil {
   409	                        return fmt.Errorf("failed to add pprof server: %w", err)
   410	                }
   411	        }
   412	
   413	        // First start any HTTP servers, which includes health probes, metrics and profiling if enabled.
   414	        //
   415	        // WARNING: HTTPServers includes the health probes, which MUST start before any cache is populated, otherwise
   416	        // it would block conversion webhooks to be ready for serving which make the cache never get ready.
   417	        logCtx := logr.NewContext(cm.internalCtx, cm.logger)
   418	        if err := cm.runnables.HTTPServers.Start(logCtx); err != nil {
   419	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start HTTP servers: %w", err)
   420	        }
   421	
   422	        // Start any webhook servers, which includes conversion, validation, and defaulting
   423	        // webhooks that are registered.
   424	        //
   425	        // WARNING: Webhooks MUST start before any cache is populated, otherwise there is a race condition
   426	        // between conversion webhooks and the cache sync (usually initial list) which causes the webhooks
   427	        // to never start because no cache can be populated.
   428	        if err := cm.runnables.Webhooks.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   429	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start webhooks: %w", err)
   430	        }
   431	
   432	        // Start and wait for caches.
   433	        if err := cm.runnables.Caches.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   434	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start caches: %w", err)
   435	        }
   436	
   437	        // Start the non-leaderelection Runnables after the cache has synced.
   438	        if err := cm.runnables.Others.Start(cm.internalCtx); err != nil {
   439	                return fmt.Errorf("failed to start other runnables: %w", err)
   440	        }
   441	
   442	        // Start the leader election and all required runnables.
   443	        {
   444	                ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
   445	                cm.leaderElectionCancel = cancel
   446	                if leaderElector != nil {
   447	                        // Start the leader elector process
   448	                        go func() {
   449	                                leaderElector.Run(ctx)
   450	                                <-ctx.Done()
   451	                                close(cm.leaderElectionStopped)
   452	                        }()
   453	                } else {
   454	                        go func() {
   455	                                // Treat not having leader election enabled the same as being elected.
   456	                                if err := cm.startLeaderElectionRunnables(); err != nil {
   457	                                        cm.errChan <- err
   458	                                }
   459	                                close(cm.elected)
   460	                        }()
   461	                }
   462	        }
   463	
   464	        ready = true
   465	        cm.Unlock()
   466	        select {
   467	        case <-ctx.Done():
   468	                // We are done
   469	                return nil
   470	        case err := <-cm.errChan:
   471	                // Error starting or running a runnable
   472	                return err
   473	        }
   474	}

Now I understand the issue better. When `ctx.Done()` is triggered at line 467, the function returns immediately. However, there might be goroutines in the runnable groups that are trying to send errors to `cm.errChan` (like in line 227 of runnable_group.go). Since the channel is unbuffered and nobody is reading from it in the `ctx.Done()` case, these goroutines will be blocked forever.

The solution is to drain the `errChan` in the `ctx.Done()` case before returning. Let me check how the channel is initialized:

2025-12-26 20:55:17,378 - INFO - swea-agent-kubernetes-sigs__controller-runtime-3247 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me write a simple test to reproduce the issue. First, let me understand what the issue is more clearly by reading the code again:

Looking at the flow:
1. When a runnable fails, it tries to send an error to `cm.errChan` (line 227 in runnable_group.go)
2. In the `Start` function (internal.go), there's a select that reads from either `ctx.Done()` or `cm.errChan`
3. If `ctx.Done()` triggers, it returns without draining `errChan`
4. This means any runnable trying to send an error to `errChan` will be blocked forever

Let me create a simple Go test to reproduce this:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_goroutine_leak.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"context"
	"fmt"
	"runtime"
	"time"

	metav1 "k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1"
	"k8s.io/client-go/rest"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager"
)

type failingRunnable struct{}

func (f *failingRunnable) Start(ctx context.Context) error {
	// Wait a bit to ensure the manager has started
	time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Return an error - this will try to send to errChan
	return fmt.Errorf("intentional error")
}

func main() {
	// Get initial goroutine count
	initialGoroutines := runtime.NumGoroutine()
	fmt.Printf("Initial goroutines: %d\n", initialGoroutines)

	// Create a test manager
	cfg := &rest.Config{
		Host: "http://localhost:8080",
	}
	
	opts := manager.Options{
		Scheme: nil,
		Logger: nil,
		LeaderElection: false,
		Metrics: manager.MetricsOptions{
			BindAddress: "0",
		},
		HealthProbeBindAddress: "0",
	}
	
	mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, opts)
	if err != nil {
		panic(fmt.Sprintf("Failed to create manager: %v", err))
	}

	// Add a runnable that will fail after a short delay
	err = mgr.Add(&failingRunnable{})
	if err != nil {
		panic(fmt.Sprintf("Failed to add runnable: %v", err))
	}

	// Create a context that will be cancelled before the runnable fails
	ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 50*time.Millisecond)
	defer cancel()

	// Start the manager - it should return when ctx is cancelled
	err = mgr.Start(ctx)
	fmt.Printf("Manager stopped with error: %v\n", err)

	// Give some time for goroutines to clean up
	time.Sleep(500 * time.Millisecond)

	// Check goroutine count
	finalGoroutines := runtime.NumGoroutine()
	fmt.Printf("Final goroutines: %d\n", finalGoroutines)
	
	// If there are leaked goroutines, report it
	if finalGoroutines > initialGoroutines {
		fmt.Printf("LEAKED GOROUTINES: %d goroutines still running\n", finalGoroutines - initialGoroutines)
		
		// Print stack traces for debugging
		buf := make([]byte, 1<<20)
		stacklen := runtime.Stack(buf, true)
		fmt.Printf("Stack traces:\n%s\n", buf[:stacklen])
	} else {
		fmt.Println("SUCCESS: No goroutine leaks detected")
	}
}
'

Now, let's understand what needs to happen. When `ctx.Done()` is triggered:
1. The deferred `engageStopProcedure` will be called (line 370)
2. Inside `engageStopProcedure`, there's already a goroutine draining `errChan` (starting at line 500)

However, the problem is that there's a race condition:
- When `ctx.Done()` triggers in the `Start` function, it returns immediately
- The deferred `engageStopProcedure` starts draining the `errChan`
- But between when the select returns and when the draining goroutine in `engageStopProcedure` starts, runnables might try to send errors

The fix should be to drain the `errChan` right after `ctx.Done()` triggers, before returning. But we need to be careful not to block forever if no errors are sent. Let me look at the `engageStopProcedure` more carefully:

2025-12-26 20:56:49,381 - INFO - swea-agent-kubernetes-sigs__controller-runtime-3247 - 💭 THOUGHT
I see. The `engageStopProcedure` function already drains the `errChan` in a goroutine. However, the issue is that this goroutine is started in `engageStopProcedure`, which is called in a defer. There's a timing issue:

1. When `ctx.Done()` happens at line 467, the function returns
2. The deferred function at line 368-381 calls `engageStopProcedure`
3. Inside `engageStopProcedure`, at line 500, a goroutine is started to drain `errChan`
4. But between step 1 and step 3, if a runnable tries to send an error to `errChan`, it will block because nobody is reading

The solution mentioned in the PR is to drain the `errChan` in the `ctx.Done()` case. Let me implement this:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/pkg/manager/internal.go   --old_str '        ready = true
        cm.Unlock()
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
                // We are done
                return nil
        case err := <-cm.errChan:
                // Error starting or running a runnable
                return err
        }' --new_str '        ready = true
        cm.Unlock()
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
                // We are done, but we need to drain any errors that might be sent
                // after we return to prevent goroutine leaks. We do this in a non-blocking
                // way by using select with default.
                select {
                case err := <-cm.errChan:
                        if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {
                                cm.logger.Error(err, "error received during shutdown")
                        }
                default:
                        // No error to drain, continue with shutdown
                }
                return nil
        case err := <-cm.errChan:
                // Error starting or running a runnable
                return err
        }'

A single non-blocking drain might not catch all errors. Let me think about this more carefully.\n\nThe issue is:\n1. Multiple runnables might be failing at the same time\n2. The `errChan` has a buffer size of 1\n3. If multiple runnables try to send errors, only one will succeed immediately (the one that fills the buffer), and the rest will block\n\nLooking at the PR description again, it says:\n> Drain the `cm.errChan` in `case <-ctx.Done()` branch\n\nAnd looking at how `engageStopProcedure` handles this (lines 500-518), it continuously drains the channel in a loop until `stopComplete` is closed.\n\nHowever, we can't just drain forever in the `ctx.Done()` case because we need to return. Wait, I realize that my approach might not be sufficient. A single non-blocking drain might not catch all errors. Let me think about this more carefully.

The issue is:
1. Multiple runnables might be failing at the same time
2. The `errChan` has a buffer size of 1
3. If multiple runnables try to send errors, only one will succeed immediately (the one that fills the buffer), and the rest will block

Looking at the PR description again, it says:
> Drain the `cm.errChan` in `case <-ctx.Done()` branch

And looking at how `engageStopProcedure` handles this (lines 500-518), it continuously drains the channel in a loop until `stopComplete` is closed.

However, we can't just drain forever in the `ctx.Done()` case because we need to return. The solution is to start draining immediately when `ctx.Done()` is triggered, and keep draining until `engageStopProcedure` takes over.

Actually, looking more carefully at the flow:
1. When `ctx.Done()` triggers, the select returns
2. The function returns
3. The deferred function calls `engageStopProcedure`
4. `engageStopProcedure` starts a goroutine to drain `errChan`

The problem is in step 2-3: there's a window where no one is draining the channel. The solution is to start draining immediately when `ctx.Done()` triggers, before returning.

Let me revise my solution to be more comprehensive:

These are Ginkgo tests. Let me think more carefully about the fix. Actually, looking at my implementation again, I realize there might be an issue. Let me trace through what happens:

1. `ctx.Done()` triggers
2. My goroutine starts and begins draining `errChan`
3. Function returns
4. Deferred `engageStopProcedure` is called
5. `engageStopProcedure` starts its own goroutine that also drains `errChan`
6. The `engageStopProcedure` goroutine immediately closes `internalProceduresStop` (line 522)
7. My goroutine detects this and exits
8. Now only the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine is draining

This looks correct, but I'm concerned about the brief period where both goroutines are draining. However, this should be fine because:
- Channel reads are atomic - only one goroutine will get each error
- Both goroutines log errors the same way
- The important thing is that errors don't block

Let me look more carefully at the `engageStopProcedure` function to see if there's a better way:

Actually, wait. Looking at the code again, I realize that `internalProceduresStop` is closed inside the `closeOnce.Do` in the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine (line 520-524). This means it's closed on the first iteration of the loop. So the timeline is:

1. `ctx.Done()` triggers
2. My goroutine starts draining
3. Function returns
4. Deferred `engageStopProcedure` is called
5. `engageStopProcedure` starts a goroutine (line 516)
6. That goroutine immediately (on first iteration) closes `internalProceduresStop` (line 522)
7. My goroutine sees `internalProceduresStop` is closed and exits
8. The `engageStopProcedure` goroutine continues draining until `stopComplete`

The window where both are draining is very small (just until the first iteration of the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine completes the `closeOnce.Do`). This should be fine.

Now let me verify my implementation doesn't introduce any other issues. Let me compile the code:

Good! It compiles. Now let me write a simple test to verify the fix works. Since the existing tests take too long, let me create a minimal test:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_fix.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"context"
	"fmt"
	"runtime"
	"time"

	"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime"
	ctrl "sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client/config"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager"
)

// SlowFailingRunnable is a runnable that fails after the context is cancelled
type SlowFailingRunnable struct{}

func (r *SlowFailingRunnable) Start(ctx context.Context) error {
	// Wait for context to be cancelled
	<-ctx.Done()
	// Then try to send an error (this would block without the fix)
	time.Sleep(10 * time.Millisecond)
	return fmt.Errorf("intentional error after context cancel")
}

func main() {
	fmt.Println("Testing goroutine leak fix...")
	
	// Record initial goroutine count
	runtime.GC()
	time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
	initialCount := runtime.NumGoroutine()
	fmt.Printf("Initial goroutines: %d\n", initialCount)
	
	// Create a manager with minimal config
	cfg, err := config.GetConfig()
	if err != nil {
		// If we can'"'"'t get a real config, create a fake one
		cfg = ctrl.GetConfigOrDie()
	}
	
	scheme := runtime.NewScheme()
	mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, manager.Options{
		Scheme: scheme,
	})
	if err != nil {
		fmt.Printf("Warning: could not create manager: %v\n", err)
		fmt.Println("This is expected if not running in a cluster")
		return
	}
	
	// Add multiple slow failing runnables
	for i := 0; i < 5; i++ {
		if err := mgr.Add(&SlowFailingRunnable{}); err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Failed to add runnable: %v\n", err)
			return
		}
	}
	
	// Create a context that will be cancelled quickly
	ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 100*time.Millisecond)
	defer cancel()
	
	// Start the manager
	fmt.Println("Starting manager...")
	startTime := time.Now()
	err = mgr.Start(ctx)
	elapsed := time.Since(startTime)
	fmt.Printf("Manager stopped after %v with error: %v\n", elapsed, err)
	
	// Give time for goroutines to clean up
	time.Sleep(500 * time.Millisecond)
	runtime.GC()
	time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Check for leaked goroutines
	finalCount := runtime.NumGoroutine()
	fmt.Printf("Final goroutines: %d\n", finalCount)
	
	leaked := finalCount - initialCount
	if leaked > 2 { // Allow for some variance
		fmt.Printf("❌ FAILED: Detected %d leaked goroutines\n", leaked)
		
		// Print stack traces
		buf := make([]byte, 1<<16)
		stacklen := runtime.Stack(buf, true)
		fmt.Printf("\n=== Goroutine stack traces ===\n%s\n", buf[:stacklen])
	} else {
		fmt.Printf("✅ SUCCESS: No significant goroutine leaks (diff: %d)\n", leaked)
	}
}
'

Good! This test already checks for context cancellation. It even has a comment "Don't leak routines" at the end. The test waits for `mgrDone` to ensure the manager has fully stopped.

Let me now think about whether my fix is complete. Looking at the PR description again, it mentions:

> When context is done, the `errChan` is not drained in ... and thus runnable groups cannot send their errors

The key issue is that when the context is cancelled, runnables might be in the middle of trying to send errors to `errChan`, and if nobody is reading from it, they'll block forever.

My fix starts a goroutine that drains `errChan` as soon as `ctx.Done()` is triggered, which should solve this issue. The goroutine continues until `engageStopProcedure` takes over.

However, I realize there's still a potential issue with my current implementation. Let me look at it again:

2025-12-26 21:01:10,796 - INFO - swea-agent-kubernetes-sigs__controller-runtime-3247 - 💭 THOUGHT
My implementation looks correct. The goroutine will:
1. Start immediately when `ctx.Done()` triggers
2. Drain `errChan` continuously
3. Stop when `internalProceduresStop` is closed (which happens very early in `engageStopProcedure`)

At that point, the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine takes over draining. This ensures continuous draining from the moment `ctx.Done()` triggers until all runnables are stopped.

Now let me think about edge cases:

**Edge case 1:** What if an error is sent to `errChan` after `internalProceduresStop` is closed but before the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine starts?
- This is not possible because `internalProceduresStop` is closed inside the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine itself, and that goroutine is already draining the channel at that point.

**Edge case 2:** What if `ctx.Done()` and an error arrive at the same time?
- The select will non-deterministically choose one. If it chooses the error, we return the error immediately. If it chooses `ctx.Done()`, we start draining and eventually the error will be read by one of the draining goroutines.

**Edge case 3:** What if the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine reads an error at the same time as my draining goroutine?
- Only one of them will successfully read the error (channel receive is atomic). Both log it the same way, so it doesn't matter which one reads it.

**Edge case 4:** What if my draining goroutine exits (because `internalProceduresStop` is closed) while there's still an error waiting in the channel?
- The `engageStopProcedure` goroutine will read it, because it continues draining until `stopComplete` is closed.

Everything looks good! Let me check if there are any other places in the code where similar issues might occur:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_simple.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"context"
	"fmt"
	"time"
)

// This is a simplified version of the issue to verify the fix works
func main() {
	// Simulating the old behavior (would deadlock)
	fmt.Println("Testing the scenario...")
	
	errChan := make(chan error, 1) // Buffered channel like in the manager
	ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
	
	// Simulate a runnable that will try to send an error after context is cancelled
	go func() {
		<-ctx.Done()
		time.Sleep(10 * time.Millisecond) // Small delay to ensure we try to send after ctx.Done() returns
		select {
		case errChan <- fmt.Errorf("runnable error"):
			fmt.Println("✅ Successfully sent error to channel (fix is working)")
		case <-time.After(100 * time.Millisecond):
			fmt.Println("❌ Timeout sending error to channel (would have deadlocked)")
		}
	}()
	
	// Wait for runnable to start
	time.Sleep(5 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Cancel the context (simulating ctx.Done() in Start function)
	cancel()
	
	// The fix: drain the channel in a goroutine
	internalProceduresStop := make(chan struct{})
	go func() {
		for {
			select {
			case err := <-errChan:
				fmt.Printf("Drained error: %v\n", err)
			case <-internalProceduresStop:
				return
			}
		}
	}()
	
	// Wait a bit for the error to be sent and drained
	time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Close the procedures stop (simulating engageStopProcedure taking over)
	close(internalProceduresStop)
	
	// Wait a bit more to ensure everything completes
	time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
	
	fmt.Println("Test completed successfully!")
}
'

2025-12-26 21:03:56,155 - INFO - swea-agent-kubernetes-sigs__controller-runtime-3247 - 💭 THOUGHT
This test suite uses envtest which requires setting up a Kubernetes environment. That's probably why the tests take so long. Let me instead verify my fix by reviewing the code logic once more and ensuring the implementation is correct.

Let me create a comprehensive summary of what I've done:

## Summary of the Fix

### Problem
When the context is cancelled (`ctx.Done()` triggers) in the `Start` function of the controller manager, it returns immediately without draining the `errChan`. Meanwhile, runnables might be trying to send errors to this channel, causing them to block forever since:
1. The channel has a buffer size of 1
2. Multiple runnables might fail at the same time
3. No one is reading from the channel after `ctx.Done()` returns

### Solution
I added code to start draining the `errChan` immediately when `ctx.Done()` triggers, before the function returns. This draining goroutine continues until `engageStopProcedure` takes over, ensuring continuous draining throughout the shutdown process.

### Implementation Details

The fix is in `/testbed/pkg/manager/internal.go`, lines 467-485:

```go
case <-ctx.Done():
    // We are done. Start draining the error channel to prevent goroutine leaks.
    // This is necessary because runnables might still be trying to send errors
    // after the context is cancelled. We'll continue draining until engageStopProcedure
    // takes over.
    go func() {
        for {
            select {
            case err := <-cm.errChan:
                if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {
                    cm.logger.Error(err, "error received during shutdown")
                }
            case <-cm.internalProceduresStop:
                // engageStopProcedure has taken over draining, we can stop
                return
            }
        }
    }()
    return nil
```

### How it Works

1. When `ctx.Done()` triggers, a goroutine is started that continuously drains `errChan`
2. The function returns, triggering the deferred `engageStopProcedure` call
3. `engageStopProcedure` starts its own goroutine (at line 516) that also drains `errChan`
4. Early in `engageStopProcedure`'s goroutine, `internalProceduresStop` is closed (line 522)
5. The first goroutine detects this and exits, leaving only `engageStopProcedure`'s goroutine to continue draining
6. The `engageStopProcedure` goroutine continues draining until all runnables are stopped (`stopComplete` is closed)

This ensures that:
- There's always someone reading from `errChan` from the moment `ctx.Done()` triggers
- Runnables can never block when trying to send errors
- No goroutines leak

Let me verify once more that the implementation is syntactically correct:

package manager_test

import (
	"context"
	"os"

	"k8s.io/client-go/rest"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/cache"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client/config"
	logf "sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/log"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager"
	"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager/signals"
)

var (
	mgr manager.Manager
	// NB: don't call SetLogger in init(), or else you'll mess up logging in the main suite.
	log = logf.Log.WithName("manager-examples")
)

// This example creates a new Manager that can be used with controller.New to create Controllers.
func ExampleNew() {
	cfg, err := config.GetConfig()
	if err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable to get kubeconfig")
		os.Exit(1)
	}

	mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, manager.Options{})
	if err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable to set up manager")
		os.Exit(1)
	}
	log.Info("created manager", "manager", mgr)
}

// This example creates a new Manager that has a cache scoped to a list of namespaces.
func ExampleNew_limitToNamespaces() {
	cfg, err := config.GetConfig()
	if err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable to get kubeconfig")
		os.Exit(1)
	}

	mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, manager.Options{
		NewCache: func(config *rest.Config, opts cache.Options) (cache.Cache, error) {
			opts.DefaultNamespaces = map[string]cache.Config{
				"namespace1": {},
				"namespace2": {},
			}
			return cache.New(config, opts)
		}},
	)
	if err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable to set up manager")
		os.Exit(1)
	}
	log.Info("created manager", "manager", mgr)
}

// This example adds a Runnable for the Manager to Start.
func ExampleManager_add() {
	err := mgr.Add(manager.RunnableFunc(func(context.Context) error {
		// Do something
		return nil
	}))
	if err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable add a runnable to the manager")
		os.Exit(1)
	}
}

// This example starts a Manager that has had Runnables added.
func ExampleManager_start() {
	if err := mgr.Start(signals.SetupSignalHandler()); err != nil {
		log.Error(err, "unable start the manager")
		os.Exit(1)
	}
}

These are just examples. Let me verify the fix is correct by reviewing the code one more time and making sure there are no edge cases I'm missing.

Let me trace through the complete flow once more:

1. **Normal operation (no ctx.Done()):**
   - Runnables run normally
   - If a runnable fails, it sends an error to `errChan`
   - The select at line 466 receives the error and returns it
   - The deferred `engageStopProcedure` is called to clean up

2. **Context cancellation (ctx.Done() triggers):**
   - The select at line 466 catches `ctx.Done()`
   - **[NEW]** A goroutine is started to drain `errChan` (line 472-484)
   - The function returns nil
   - The deferred `engageStopProcedure` is called
   - `engageStopProcedure` starts its own draining goroutine (line 516)
   - **[NEW]** The first goroutine exits when `internalProceduresStop` is closed
   - The `engageStopProcedure` goroutine continues draining until complete

This looks correct! The key insight is that my new goroutine provides a "bridge" - it starts draining immediately when `ctx.Done()` triggers and continues until `engageStopProcedure` takes over.

+		// This is necessary because runnables might still be trying to send errors
+		// after the context is cancelled. We'll continue draining until engageStopProcedure
+		// takes over.
+		go func() {
+			for {
+				select {
+				case err := <-cm.errChan:
+					if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {
+						cm.logger.Error(err, "error received during shutdown")
+					}
+				case <-cm.internalProceduresStop:
+					// engageStopProcedure has taken over draining, we can stop
+					return
+				}
+			}
+		}()

Perfect! No vet issues. Let me also double-check that the fix handles all the scenarios mentioned in the PR:

## Verification of the Fix

### PR Description Analysis:

The PR describes the issue:
1. ✅ `controllerManager` passes its `errChan` to its `runnableGroup`s - **Confirmed in code**
2. ✅ When runnables fail, they send errors to `errChan` at line 227 of runnable_group.go - **Confirmed**
3. ✅ When context is done, `errChan` is not drained - **Fixed by my change**
4. ✅ Runnable groups cannot send their errors and block forever - **Fixed by my change**

### The Fix:

My implementation adds a goroutine that starts draining `errChan` immediately when `ctx.Done()` triggers, preventing any runnables from blocking when trying to send errors. The goroutine continues draining until `engageStopProcedure` takes over, ensuring continuous draining throughout the shutdown process.

Perfect! `internalProceduresStop` is initialized during manager creation, so it's safe to use in my new goroutine.

Let me now think about whether there are any other edge cases:

### Edge Case Analysis:

1. **What if `ctx.Done()` happens before any runnables are started?**
   - The draining goroutine will start, but there will be no errors to drain
   - `engageStopProcedure` will be called and close `internalProceduresStop`
   - The draining goroutine will exit cleanly
   - ✅ No issue

2. **What if `engageStopProcedure` is called multiple times?**
   - There's already protection: `atomic.CompareAndSwapInt64(cm.stopProcedureEngaged, 0, 1)` at line 495
   - This ensures `engageStopProcedure` is only executed once
   - ✅ No issue

3. **What if both my goroutine and the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine try to read from `errChan` simultaneously?**
   - Channel receives are atomic - only one will succeed
   - Both log errors the same way, so it doesn't matter which one reads it
   - ✅ No issue

4. **What if `internalProceduresStop` is closed while my goroutine is blocked on reading from `errChan`?**
   - The select will detect the closure on the next iteration
   - If an error was received first, it will be logged, then the goroutine will exit on the next iteration
   - ✅ No issue

5. **What if there are multiple errors in `errChan`?**
   - The channel has a buffer of 1, so at most 1 error is buffered
   - Other senders will block until someone reads
   - My goroutine (and then the `engageStopProcedure` goroutine) continuously reads, so senders won't block
   - ✅ No issue

All edge cases are handled correctly!

Let me create one final test to verify the logic is sound:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_comprehensive.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"context"
	"fmt"
	"sync"
	"time"
)

// Comprehensive test of the draining mechanism
func main() {
	fmt.Println("=== Testing comprehensive draining scenario ===\n")
	
	errChan := make(chan error, 1)
	internalProceduresStop := make(chan struct{})
	stopComplete := make(chan struct{})
	
	// Simulate multiple runnables trying to send errors after context cancellation
	var wg sync.WaitGroup
	for i := 0; i < 5; i++ {
		wg.Add(1)
		go func(id int) {
			defer wg.Done()
			time.Sleep(time.Duration(id*5) * time.Millisecond)
			
			// Try to send error
			select {
			case errChan <- fmt.Errorf("error from runnable %d", id):
				fmt.Printf("✅ Runnable %d: successfully sent error\n", id)
			case <-time.After(100 * time.Millisecond):
				fmt.Printf("❌ Runnable %d: TIMEOUT sending error (would have leaked)\n", id)
			}
		}(i)
	}
	
	// Simulate the first draining goroutine (from ctx.Done() case)
	go func() {
		fmt.Println("Starting first draining goroutine (ctx.Done() case)")
		for {
			select {
			case err := <-errChan:
				fmt.Printf("  First drainer: received %v\n", err)
			case <-internalProceduresStop:
				fmt.Println("First draining goroutine: stopping (engageStopProcedure took over)")
				return
			}
		}
	}()
	
	// Wait a bit for some errors to be sent
	time.Sleep(30 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Close internalProceduresStop (simulating engageStopProcedure starting)
	close(internalProceduresStop)
	fmt.Println("\nengageStopProcedure: taking over")
	
	// Simulate the engageStopProcedure draining goroutine
	go func() {
		fmt.Println("Starting engageStopProcedure draining goroutine")
		for {
			select {
			case err := <-errChan:
				fmt.Printf("  engageStopProcedure drainer: received %v\n", err)
			case <-stopComplete:
				fmt.Println("engageStopProcedure draining goroutine: stopping (all done)")
				return
			}
		}
	}()
	
	// Wait for all runnables to finish
	wg.Wait()
	fmt.Println("\nAll runnables finished")
	
	// Give time for any remaining errors to be drained
	time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
	
	// Signal complete
	close(stopComplete)
	fmt.Println("Shutdown complete")
	
	// Wait a bit for goroutines to exit
	time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
	
	fmt.Println("\n✅ Test completed successfully - no goroutine leaks!")
}
'

+package main
+
+import (
+"fmt"
+"sync"
+"time"
+)
+
+// Comprehensive test of the draining mechanism
+func main() {
+fmt.Println("=== Testing comprehensive draining scenario ===\n")
+
+errChan := make(chan error, 1)
+internalProceduresStop := make(chan struct{})
+stopComplete := make(chan struct{})
+
+// Simulate multiple runnables trying to send errors after context cancellation
+var wg sync.WaitGroup
+for i := 0; i < 5; i++ {
+wg.Add(1)
+go func(id int) {
+defer wg.Done()
+time.Sleep(time.Duration(id*5) * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Try to send error
+select {
+case errChan <- fmt.Errorf("error from runnable %d", id):
+fmt.Printf("✅ Runnable %d: successfully sent error\n", id)
+case <-time.After(100 * time.Millisecond):
+fmt.Printf("❌ Runnable %d: TIMEOUT sending error (would have leaked)\n", id)
+}
+}(i)
+}
+
+// Simulate the first draining goroutine (from ctx.Done() case)
+go func() {
+fmt.Println("Starting first draining goroutine (ctx.Done() case)")
+for {
+select {
+case err := <-errChan:
+fmt.Printf("  First drainer: received %v\n", err)
+case <-internalProceduresStop:
+fmt.Println("First draining goroutine: stopping (engageStopProcedure took over)")
+return
+}
+}
+}()
+
+// Wait a bit for some errors to be sent
+time.Sleep(30 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Close internalProceduresStop (simulating engageStopProcedure starting)
+close(internalProceduresStop)
+fmt.Println("\nengageStopProcedure: taking over")
+
+// Simulate the engageStopProcedure draining goroutine
+go func() {
+fmt.Println("Starting engageStopProcedure draining goroutine")
+for {
+select {
+case err := <-errChan:
+fmt.Printf("  engageStopProcedure drainer: received %v\n", err)
+case <-stopComplete:
+fmt.Println("engageStopProcedure draining goroutine: stopping (all done)")
+return
+}
+}
+}()
+
+// Wait for all runnables to finish
+wg.Wait()
+fmt.Println("\nAll runnables finished")
+
+// Give time for any remaining errors to be drained
+time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Signal complete
+close(stopComplete)
+fmt.Println("Shutdown complete")
+
+// Wait a bit for goroutines to exit
+time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
+
+fmt.Println("\n✅ Test completed successfully - no goroutine leaks!")
+}
diff --git a/test_fix.go b/test_fix.go
new file mode 100644
index 00000000..2fff429c

+++ b/test_fix.go
@@ -0,0 +1,91 @@
+package main
+
+import (
+"context"
+"fmt"
+"runtime"
+"time"
+
+"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime"
+ctrl "sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime"
+"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/client/config"
+"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager"
+)
+
+// SlowFailingRunnable is a runnable that fails after the context is cancelled
+type SlowFailingRunnable struct{}
+
+func (r *SlowFailingRunnable) Start(ctx context.Context) error {
+// Wait for context to be cancelled
+<-ctx.Done()
+// Then try to send an error (this would block without the fix)
+time.Sleep(10 * time.Millisecond)
+return fmt.Errorf("intentional error after context cancel")
+}
+
+func main() {
+fmt.Println("Testing goroutine leak fix...")
+
+// Record initial goroutine count
+runtime.GC()
+time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
+initialCount := runtime.NumGoroutine()
+fmt.Printf("Initial goroutines: %d\n", initialCount)
+
+// Create a manager with minimal config
+cfg, err := config.GetConfig()
+if err != nil {
+// If we can't get a real config, create a fake one
+cfg = ctrl.GetConfigOrDie()
+}
+
+scheme := runtime.NewScheme()
+mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, manager.Options{
+Scheme: scheme,
+})
+if err != nil {
+fmt.Printf("Warning: could not create manager: %v\n", err)
+fmt.Println("This is expected if not running in a cluster")
+return
+}
+
+// Add multiple slow failing runnables
+for i := 0; i < 5; i++ {
+if err := mgr.Add(&SlowFailingRunnable{}); err != nil {
+fmt.Printf("Failed to add runnable: %v\n", err)
+return
+}
+}
+
+// Create a context that will be cancelled quickly
+ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 100*time.Millisecond)
+defer cancel()
+
+// Start the manager
+fmt.Println("Starting manager...")
+startTime := time.Now()
+err = mgr.Start(ctx)
+elapsed := time.Since(startTime)
+fmt.Printf("Manager stopped after %v with error: %v\n", elapsed, err)
+
+// Give time for goroutines to clean up
+time.Sleep(500 * time.Millisecond)
+runtime.GC()
+time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Check for leaked goroutines
+finalCount := runtime.NumGoroutine()
+fmt.Printf("Final goroutines: %d\n", finalCount)
+
+leaked := finalCount - initialCount
+if leaked > 2 { // Allow for some variance
+fmt.Printf("❌ FAILED: Detected %d leaked goroutines\n", leaked)
+
+// Print stack traces
+buf := make([]byte, 1<<16)
+stacklen := runtime.Stack(buf, true)
+fmt.Printf("\n=== Goroutine stack traces ===\n%s\n", buf[:stacklen])
+} else {
+fmt.Printf("✅ SUCCESS: No significant goroutine leaks (diff: %d)\n", leaked)
+}
+}

+package main
+
+import (
+"context"
+"fmt"
+"runtime"
+"time"
+
+"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime"
+"k8s.io/client-go/rest"
+ctrl "sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime"
+"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager"
+)
+
+type failingRunnable struct{}
+
+func (f *failingRunnable) Start(ctx context.Context) error {
+// Wait a bit to ensure the manager has started
+time.Sleep(100 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Return an error - this will try to send to errChan
+return fmt.Errorf("intentional error")
+}
+
+func main() {
+// Get initial goroutine count
+initialGoroutines := runtime.NumGoroutine()
+fmt.Printf("Initial goroutines: %d\n", initialGoroutines)
+
+// Create a test manager
+cfg := &rest.Config{
+Host: "http://localhost:8080",
+}
+
+opts := manager.Options{
+Scheme: runtime.NewScheme(),
+Logger: ctrl.Log.WithName("test"),
+LeaderElection: false,
+}
+
+mgr, err := manager.New(cfg, opts)
+if err != nil {
+panic(fmt.Sprintf("Failed to create manager: %v", err))
+}
+
+// Add a runnable that will fail after a short delay
+err = mgr.Add(&failingRunnable{})
+if err != nil {
+panic(fmt.Sprintf("Failed to add runnable: %v", err))
+}
+
+// Create a context that will be cancelled before the runnable fails
+ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 50*time.Millisecond)
+defer cancel()
+
+// Start the manager - it should return when ctx is cancelled
+err = mgr.Start(ctx)
+fmt.Printf("Manager stopped with error: %v\n", err)
+
+// Give some time for goroutines to clean up
+time.Sleep(500 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Check goroutine count
+finalGoroutines := runtime.NumGoroutine()
+fmt.Printf("Final goroutines: %d\n", finalGoroutines)
+
+// If there are leaked goroutines, report it
+if finalGoroutines > initialGoroutines {
+fmt.Printf("LEAKED GOROUTINES: %d goroutines still running\n", finalGoroutines - initialGoroutines)
+
+// Print stack traces for debugging
+buf := make([]byte, 1<<20)
+stacklen := runtime.Stack(buf, true)
+fmt.Printf("Stack traces:\n%s\n", buf[:stacklen])
+} else {
+fmt.Println("SUCCESS: No goroutine leaks detected")
+}
+}

+package main
+
+import (
+"context"
+"fmt"
+"time"
+)
+
+// This is a simplified version of the issue to verify the fix works
+func main() {
+// Simulating the old behavior (would deadlock)
+fmt.Println("Testing the scenario...")
+
+errChan := make(chan error, 1) // Buffered channel like in the manager
+ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
+
+// Simulate a runnable that will try to send an error after context is cancelled
+go func() {
+<-ctx.Done()
+time.Sleep(10 * time.Millisecond) // Small delay to ensure we try to send after ctx.Done() returns
+select {
+case errChan <- fmt.Errorf("runnable error"):
+fmt.Println("✅ Successfully sent error to channel (fix is working)")
+case <-time.After(100 * time.Millisecond):
+fmt.Println("❌ Timeout sending error to channel (would have deadlocked)")
+}
+}()
+
+// Wait for runnable to start
+time.Sleep(5 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Cancel the context (simulating ctx.Done() in Start function)
+cancel()
+
+// The fix: drain the channel in a goroutine
+internalProceduresStop := make(chan struct{})
+go func() {
+for {
+select {
+case err := <-errChan:
+fmt.Printf("Drained error: %v\n", err)
+case <-internalProceduresStop:
+return
+}
+}
+}()
+
+// Wait a bit for the error to be sent and drained
+time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
+
+// Close the procedures stop (simulating engageStopProcedure taking over)
+close(internalProceduresStop)
+
+// Wait a bit more to ensure everything completes
+time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
+
+fmt.Println("Test completed successfully!")
+}

</diff>
